<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Yahtzee</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">This article is about the dice game. For the video game journalist, see <a href="/wiki/Ben_%22Yahtzee%22_Croshaw" title='Ben "Yahtzee" Croshaw'>Ben "Yahtzee" Croshaw</a>.</div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em">

<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yahtzee_logo.svg"><img alt="Yahtzee logo.svg" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="158" height="60" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Yahtzee_logo.svg/158px-Yahtzee_logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Yahtzee_logo.svg/237px-Yahtzee_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Yahtzee_logo.svg/316px-Yahtzee_logo.svg.png 2x" width="158"/></a>

</table>
<p><i><b>Yahtzee</b></i> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dice_game" title="Dice game">dice game</a> made by <a href="/wiki/Milton_Bradley_Company" title="Milton Bradley Company">Milton Bradley</a> (now owned by <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a>), which was first marketed as "Yatzie" by <b>National Association Service</b> of Toledo, Ohio, in the early 1940s. Yatzie was included in a game set called "LUCK - 15 Grand Dice Games". It was marketed under the name of Yahtzee by game entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Edwin_S._Lowe" title="Edwin S. Lowe">Edwin S. Lowe</a> in 1956. Lowe is also responsible for introducing Bingo to the U.S. market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The game is a development of earlier dice games such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poker_Dice" title="Poker Dice">Poker Dice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yacht_(dice_game)" title="Yacht (dice game)">Yacht</a> and <a href="/wiki/Generala" title="Generala">Generala</a>. It is also similar to <a href="/wiki/Yatzy" title="Yatzy">Yatzy</a>, which is popular in Scandinavia.</p>
<p>The object of the game is to score points by rolling five <a href="/wiki/Dice" title="Dice">dice</a> to make certain combinations. The dice can be rolled up to three times in a turn to try to make various scoring combinations. A game consists of thirteen rounds. After each round the player chooses which scoring category is to be used for that round. Once a category has been used in the game, it cannot be used again. The scoring categories have varying point values, some of which are fixed values and others where the score depends on the value of the dice. A <b>Yahtzee</b> is five-of-a-kind and scores 50 points; the highest of any category. The winner is the player who scores the most points.</p>
<p>Yahtzee was marketed by the E.S. Lowe Company from 1956 till 1973. In 1973, the <a href="/wiki/Milton_Bradley_Company" title="Milton Bradley Company">Milton Bradley Company</a> purchased the E.S. Lowe Company and assumed the rights to produce and sell Yahtzee. During <a href="/wiki/Edwin_S._Lowe" title="Edwin S. Lowe">Lowe's</a> ownership over 40 million Yahtzee games were sold worldwide. The game has maintained its popularity. According to current owner <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a>, 50 million Yahtzee games are sold each year. A classic edition is currently being marketed by <a href="/wiki/Winning_Moves" title="Winning Moves">Winning Moves</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yahtzee_1956.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="649" data-file-width="810" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/Yahtzee_1956.JPG/220px-Yahtzee_1956.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/Yahtzee_1956.JPG/330px-Yahtzee_1956.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0f/Yahtzee_1956.JPG/440px-Yahtzee_1956.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yahtzee_1956.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Original 1956 Yahtzee Board Game</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The overall concept of Yahtzee traces its roots to a number of traditional dice games. Among these is the Puerto Rican game <a href="/wiki/Generala" title="Generala">Generala</a>, and the English games of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poker_Dice" title="Poker Dice">Poker Dice</a> and Cheerio. Another game, Yap, shows close similarities to Yahtzee; this game was copyrighted by Robert Cissne in 1952.</p>
<p>The most important predecessor of Yahtzee is the dice game named "<a href="/wiki/Yacht_(dice_game)" title="Yacht (dice game)">Yacht</a>", which is an English cousin of Generala and dates back to at least 1938.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-2">[2]</a></sup> Wood<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-2">[2]</a></sup> classifies Yacht, and a similar three-dice game called Crag, as sequence dice games. Yahtzee is similar to Yacht in both name and content. Although Yahtzee is clearly derived from Yacht, it differed from it in a number of significant ways:</p>
<ul>
<li>It introduced the upper section bonus.</li>
<li>It included the three-of-a-kind category.</li>
<li>In Yacht both straights are a sequence of five ("Big Straight" is 2-3-4-5-6, "Little Straight" is 1-2-3-4-5). Yahtzee introduced the sequence of four straight (the "Small Straight").</li>
<li>It introduced Yahtzee bonuses and the Joker rule.</li>
</ul>
<p>There were also a number of scoring differences. The present-day commercial Yahtzee began when toy and game entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Edwin_S._Lowe" title="Edwin S. Lowe">Edwin S. Lowe</a> filed Yahtzee as a trademark with the U.S. Patent Office on April 19, 1956. The first commercial usage of the name Yahtzee was a few weeks earlier on April 3. <a href="/wiki/Edwin_S._Lowe" title="Edwin S. Lowe">Lowe</a> classified his product as a "Poker Dice Game."</p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a>, the game was invented by an anonymous Canadian couple, who called it "The Yacht Game" because they played it on their yacht with their friends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hasbro_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-hasbro-3">[3]</a></sup> Later they asked Lowe if he would make up some sets to be given as gifts to their friends who enjoyed the game. Lowe perceived the possibility of marketing the game, and acquired the rights to the game from the couple in exchange for 1,000 gift sets. This story is expanded by <a href="/wiki/Edwin_S._Lowe" title="Edwin S. Lowe">Lowe</a> in the 1973 book, <i>A Toy is Born</i> by Marvin Kaye. According to Lowe, the game did not initially do well commercially, since the rules and appeal were not easily conveyed in an advertisement. Eventually, he had the idea of organizing Yahtzee parties at which people could play the game and thereby gain a first-hand appreciation of it. The idea was successful, and enthusiasts quickly popularized the game through word of mouth.</p>
<p>The E.S. Lowe Company sold Yahtzee from 1956 to 1973. During <a href="/wiki/Edwin_S._Lowe" title="Edwin S. Lowe">Lowe's</a> ownership, a number of changes were made to the game's packaging, contents, and appearance. Between 1956 and 1961, the game's advertising slogan was changed from "The Game That Makes You <i>Think</i> While Having <i>Fun</i>" to "The <i>Fun</i> Game That Makes <i>Thinking</i> Fun!"</p>
<p>The game and its contents were copyrighted by Lowe in 1956, 1961, 1967, and 1972. In 1973, <a href="/wiki/Milton_Bradley_Company" title="Milton Bradley Company">Milton Bradley</a> purchased the E.S. Lowe Company and assumed the rights to produce and sell Yahtzee. During Lowe's ownership over 40 million Yahtzee games were sold in America and around the globe. The game has maintained its popularity. According to current owner <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a>, 50 million Yahtzee games are sold each year.</p>
<p>Over time, the Yahtzee logo has taken several forms. The original version of the logo was used throughout the entire period that the game was produced solely by the Lowe company. After 1973, the logo changed various times. This logo is found on the scorecards and the game box(es).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rules">Rules</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Rules">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yahtzee_logo.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="95" data-file-width="256" height="82" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/eb/Yahtzee_logo.JPG/220px-Yahtzee_logo.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/eb/Yahtzee_logo.JPG 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yahtzee_logo.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo of the game as originally published in 1954. It includes a caricature of E. S. Lowe, the person responsible for the game's production.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The game consists of a number of rounds. In each round, a player gets three rolls of the dice, although they can choose to end their turn after one or two rolls. After the first roll the player can save any dice they want and re-roll the other dice. This procedure is repeated after the second roll. The player has complete choice as to which dice to roll. They can re-roll a die for the third roll that was not rolled on the second roll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Yahtzee scorecard contains 13 different category boxes and in each round, after the third roll, the player must choose one of these categories. The score entered in the box depends on how well the five dice match the scoring rule for the category. Details of the scoring rules for each category are given below. As an example, one of the categories is called Three of a Kind. The scoring rule for this category means that a player only scores if at least three of the five dice are the same value. The game is completed after 13 rounds by each player, with each of the 13 boxes filled. The total score is calculated by summing all thirteen boxes, together with any bonuses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Yahtzee scorecard contains 13 scoring boxes divided between two sections: the <b>upper section</b> and the <b>lower section</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Upper_section">Upper section</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Upper section">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the upper section there are six boxes. The score in each of these boxes is determined by adding the total number of dice matching that box.</p>

<p>If a player scores a total of 63 or more points in these six boxes, a bonus of 35 is added to the upper section score. Although 63 points corresponds to scoring exactly three-of-a-kind for each of the six boxes, a common way to get the bonus is by scoring four-of-a-kind for some numbers so that fewer of other numbers are needed. A player can earn the bonus even if they score a "0" in an upper section box.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In order to gauge how well a player is doing in the upper section, they often refer to being "up" or "down" compared to the average of three required for each box. So that if a player scores four "sixes" they will be "6 up"; while if they then score just two "twos" they will then be only "4 up". Similarly, if a player starts with two "twos" they will be "2 down".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lower_section">Lower section</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Lower section">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The lower section contains a number of poker-themed categories with specific point values:</p>

<p>Some players count a Yahtzee as being a valid Full House. However the official rule is that a Full House is "three of one number and two of another".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Small Straight and Large Straight are sometimes called by different names, either <b>Low Straight</b> and <b>High Straight</b>, <b>Short Straight</b> and <b>Long Straight</b> or <b>Little Straight</b> and <b>Big Straight</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>If a category is chosen but the dice do not match the requirements of the category the player scores 0 in that category. Some combinations offer the player a choice as to which category to score them under; e.g., a full house could be scored in the Full House, the Three-Of-A-Kind, or the Chance categories. The Chance category is often used for a turn that will not score well in any other category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-7"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
<div class="thumbimage" style="width:200px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yahtzee_components.jpg"><img alt="Yahtzee components.jpg" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b3/Yahtzee_components.jpg/200px-Yahtzee_components.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b3/Yahtzee_components.jpg/300px-Yahtzee_components.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b3/Yahtzee_components.jpg/400px-Yahtzee_components.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a><br/>
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Five_ivory_dice.jpg"><img alt="Five ivory dice.jpg" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Five_ivory_dice.jpg/200px-Five_ivory_dice.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Five_ivory_dice.jpg/300px-Five_ivory_dice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Five_ivory_dice.jpg/400px-Five_ivory_dice.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">Although Yahtzee is a commercial game with its own components (game set in upper image), the game can also be played with just five dice (such as the dice in the lower image), some pencils or pens and sheets of paper, and the knowledge of the rules and scoring categories.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yahtzee_bonuses_and_Joker_rules">Yahtzee bonuses and Joker rules</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Yahtzee bonuses and Joker rules">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <i>Yahtzee</i> occurs when all five dice are the same. If a player throws a Yahtzee but the Yahtzee category has already been used, special rules apply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-8"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>If the player throws a Yahtzee and has already filled the Yahtzee box with a score of 50, they score a Yahtzee bonus and get an extra 100 points. However, if they throw a Yahtzee and have filled the Yahtzee category with a score of 0, they do not get a Yahtzee bonus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-9"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In either case they then select a category, as usual. Scoring is the same as normal except that, if the Upper Section box corresponding to the Yahtzee has been used, the Full House, Small Straight and Large Straight categories can be used to score 25, 30 or 40 (respectively) even though the dice do not meet the normal requirement for those categories. In this case the Yahtzee is said to act as a "Joker".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-10"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are two alternative versions of the Joker rule used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-11"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Forced_Joker_rule">Forced Joker rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Forced Joker rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the official rules<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-12"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup> the player must act in the following way.</p>
<ul>
<li>If the corresponding Upper Section box is unused then that category must be used.</li>
<li>If the corresponding Upper Section box has been used already, a Lower Section box must be used. The Yahtzee acts as a Joker so that the Full House, Small Straight and Large Straight categories can be used to score 25, 30 or 40 (respectively).</li>
<li>If the corresponding Upper Section box and all Lower Section boxes have been used an unused Upper Section box must be used, scoring 0.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_choice_Joker_rule">Free choice Joker rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Free choice Joker rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the simpler, alternative version of the Joker rule<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vancura_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-vancura-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vslides2_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-vslides2-6">[6]</a></sup> the player retains the free choice as to which category to use, but the Yahtzee can only be used as a Joker if the corresponding Upper Section box has been used. If the corresponding Upper Section box is unused the Yahtzee would score 0 if the Full House, Small Straight or Large Straight categories were chosen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-13"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_Joker_rule">Original Joker rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Original Joker rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The original game rules released in 1956 contain a difference from the above rules. The booklet stated that additional Yahtzees must be used as Jokers in the Lower Section and did not allow for their use in the Upper Section. This rule was changed when the game was re-copyrighted in 1961.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-14"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The winner is the player with the highest total. The rules do not specify what happens in the event of a tie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_4-15"><a href="#cite_note-rules-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Example_games">Example games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Example games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategies">Strategies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Strategies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A detailed discussion of the optimal strategy is beyond the scope of this article but certain aspects can be considered here.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Completing_a_Yahtzee">Completing a Yahtzee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Completing a Yahtzee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>It is important to understand the probability of completing a Yahtzee. This depends on whether a particular Yahtzee is required or any Yahtzee.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Specific_Yahtzee">Specific Yahtzee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Specific Yahtzee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The probability of completing a specific Yahtzee is shown in the following table.</p>

<p>So if a three-of-a-kind is thrown on the first roll, the chance of completing a Yahtzee increases from 4.60% to 9.34%.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_round">Final round</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Final round">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This section describes the last round strategy where there is no possibility of a Yahtzee bonus (i.e. there is a score of 0 in the Yahtzee box). These are the simplest situations to analyse, although even at this late stage the strategy may vary depending on the game situation.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Upper_Section_box">Upper Section box</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Upper Section box">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>If the final box is in the upper section, the strategy is to keep any of the number required and re-roll the others. On average 2.11 of the number required will be gotten, scoring from 2.11 (for 1s) to 12.64 (for 6s). The distribution is as follows:</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">
<tr>
<th>Total</th>
<th>Probability</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>At least 1</td>
<td>93.51%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>At least 2</td>
<td>69.88%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>At least 3</td>
<td>35.48%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>At least 4</td>
<td>10.44%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>5</td>
<td>1.33%</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Three-Of-A-Kind">Three-Of-A-Kind</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Three-Of-A-Kind">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are slightly different strategies depending on whether a player is simply just trying to get a three-of-a-kind or if they are trying to maximize their average score. Different strategies will also be required should a specific target be needed to achieve.</p>
<p>The strategy to maximize the chance of getting a three-of-a-kind involves keeping any three-of-a-kind that is rolled. If a three-of-a-kind is rolled then after the first throw the player should keep any other 5s and 6s, while after the second throw the player should keep any other 4s, 5s, and 6s. An example is with 22225 the player keeps 2225 and throws the other 2. If a three-of-a-kind is not rolled the player should keep any pair that is rolled and re-roll the other dice, with two pairs the player should keep the higher pair, and with no pair the player should keep the highest die. Following this strategy gives a 74.32% chance of getting a three-of-a-kind.</p>
<p>This strategy does not maximize the average score since there are a few situations after the first throw, where it is better to keep other combinations. For instance after throwing 11166, keeping 11166 maximizes the chance of getting a three-of-a-kind (a guaranteed score of 15) but keeping 66 maximizes the expected average score (17.54), although it introduces a significant<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (June 2016)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup> chance of scoring nothing. The situations where the strategy to maximize the average score differs are all after the first throw and are as follows: keep 33, 44, 55, 66 rather than 111 (or 11155, 11166), keep 4, 5 or 6 rather than 11, keep 5 or 6 rather than 22, keep 336 rather than 33. For example, with 22456 the player should keep 6 rather than 22 and with 33456 he should keep 336 not 33.If he follows the strategy to maximize the average score he will get a three-of-a-kind 71.51% of the time and score an average of 15.19.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Four-Of-A-Kind">Four-Of-A-Kind</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Four-Of-A-Kind">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As with three-of-a-kind there are slightly different strategies depending on whether a player is simply trying to get a four-of-a-kind or he is trying to maximize his average score. Different strategies will also be required should he need to achieve a specific target.</p>
<p>The strategy to maximize his chance of getting a four-of-a-kind involves keeping any four-of-a-kind that he has. If he has a four-of-a-kind then after the first throw he will keep the other if it is a 5 and 6, while after the second throw he will keep it if it is a 4, 5 or 6. So that with 22223 he keeps 2222 and will throw the 3. If he does not have a four-of-a-kind, the player should keep any three-of-a-kind or pair that he has and re-roll the other dice. With two pairs he will keep the higher pair. With no pair he will keep the highest die. Following this strategy gives him a 29.08% chance of getting a four-of-a-kind.</p>
<p>As with three-of-a-kind this strategy does not maximize the average score since there are a few situations after the first throw, where it is better to keep other combinations. For instance, after throwing 11166, keeping 111 maximizes the chance of getting a four-of-a-kind but keeping 66 maximizes the expected average score (6.20 rather than 4.18). The situations where the strategy to maximize the average score differs are all after the first throw and are as follows: keep 44, 55, 66 rather than 111, keep 4, 5 or 6 rather than 11, keep 6 rather than 22. Following the strategy to maximize the average score he will get a four-of-a-kind 27.74% of the time and score an average of 5.61.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Full_House">Full House</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Full House">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A player will keep a Yahtzee or Full House. A Yahtzee will score 25 under the Joker rule, even though it is not strictly a full house.he will keep any four-of-a-kind, three-of-a-kind or pairs that are thrown and re-roll the others. With two pairs he will keep both. On average he will succeed 36.61% of the time and score an average of 9.15.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Small_Straight">Small Straight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Small Straight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The strategy is complicated by the fact that, because of the Joker rule, the player will score 30 if he gets a Yahtzee. Clearly he keeps any Small Straight or Yahtzee that he throws. After the first throw he will keep a run of 3 or 3 out of 4 (e.g. 124) if he has one. Otherwise he will keep a 3 or 4 (or both) and a 2 or 5 if he also has a 3 or 4 (e.g. with 11245 he will keep 24 but with 11255 he will keep nothing).He will not keep just 2, 5 or 25. The only difference after the second throw is that he keeps 1111, 2222, 5555 and 6666 and will try to throw a Yahtzee unless the other die is a 3 or 4.</p>
<p>On average he will succeed 61.60% of the time and score an average of 18.48.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Large_Straight">Large Straight</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Large Straight">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Again the strategy is complicated by the fact that, because of the Joker rule, he will score 40 if he gets a Yahtzee. Clearly he will keep any Large Straight or Yahtzee that he throws. The best strategy is also to keep a four-of-a-kind and try to throw a Yahtzee, even after the first throw.The player should not keep a three-of-a-kind. Keep a small straight or 4 out of 5 (e.g. 1235) if he has one. Otherwise he should simply keep any 2, 3, 4 or 5 (just one of each), so that with 12256 he would keep 25.</p>
<p>On average he will succeed 26.53% of the time and score an average of 10.61.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Yahtzee">Yahtzee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Yahtzee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A player should keep any Yahtzee, four-of-a-kind, three-of-a-kind or pair that is thrown and re-roll the others. On average he will succeed 4.60% of the time and score an average of 2.30.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chance">Chance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Chance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>To get the maximum average score the strategy is straightforward. After the first throw the player will keep any 5s and 6s. After the second throw he will keep any 4s, 5s, and 6s. On average he will score 23.33. Different strategies will be required when he needs to achieve a specific target.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Optimal_strategy">Optimal strategy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Optimal strategy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The strategy for maximizing the <a href="/wiki/Expected_value" title="Expected value">expected</a> score has been determined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vancura_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-vancura-5">[5]</a></sup> The average score when using this strategy is 254.59.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vslides2_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-vslides2-6">[6]</a></sup> This average is based on calculations using the "free choice Joker rule".</p>
<p>It is important to note that the "Optimal" strategy simply maximises the average score. It does not maximise the chances of winning a game. There are two main reasons for this.</p>
<p>Firstly, the Optimal strategy takes no account of any opponents. In normal gameplay a player will adjust their strategy depending on the scores of the other player or players.</p>
<p>Secondly, the Optimal strategy tends to give undue importance to Yahtzee bonuses. It is rare for a player without a Yahtzee bonus to beat a player with one. So, in normal gameplay, a players' strategy is not significantly influenced by the value given for a Yahtzee bonus. Consider the situation where the Yahtzee bonus was worth a million rather than a hundred. It would not influence normal gameplay where the objective is to score more than the opponent. It would, however, affect the "Optimal" strategy since scoring a million would have a dramatic effect on the average score. The "Optimal" strategy would be dominated by the prospect of a Yahtzee bonus. Even with a Yahtzee bonus worth 100 the "Optimal" strategy tends to give too much importance to Yahtzee bonuses.</p>
<p>Despite these limitations the "Optimal" strategy does provide a useful guide as to the best strategy, especially in the early rounds. The "Optimal" strategy for the first round is described in the next section. After the first round, the number of different games rapidly makes detailed analysis difficult but, in the early rounds, players generally simply adapt the first round strategy based on the boxes used. For instance if a player throws 15566 in the first round they will keep 66 but if the 6s box was used in the first round and they throw 15566 in the second round they will naturally keep 55 instead.</p>

<td>Small Straight</td>
<td>29.46</td>
<td>1.80%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Large Straight</td>
<td>32.71</td>
<td>18.22%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Yahtzee</td>
<td>16.87</td>
<td>66.26%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Chance</td>
<td>22.01</td>
<td>-</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Yahtzee Bonus</td>
<td>9.58</td>
<td>91.76%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>TOTAL</td>
<td>254.59</td>
<td>-</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The bonus is made in 68% of games but in only 1% of games does the player get exactly 3-of-a-kind of each Upper Section category. In a further 5% of games the player gets at least 3-of-a-kind in each of these categories and 4-of-a-kind in one or more of them. In the remaining 62% of games, there is at least one category which scores a pair or less but the bonus is achieved by scoring one or more 4-of-a-kind in the Upper Section. It is possible to calculate the maximum average score with different rules. When the rules are changed so that there is no Upper Section bonus the average score drops from 254.59 to 237.84, a reduction of 16.75. This compares with an average bonus score of 23.84 and shows that changes to the strategy to improve the chance of getting the bonus are to the detriment of the other scores; the average score in the other boxes drops by 7.09.</p>
<p>A Yahtzee is scored in about 34% of games while a Yahtzee bonus is scored in about 8% of games. A second Yahtzee bonus occurs about 1% of the time while a third one is scored in about 0.1% of games. The average number of Yahtzees thrown in a game is 0.46.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vslides2_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-vslides2-6">[6]</a></sup> This includes about 3% of games where a Yahtzee is thrown after 0 has been scored in the Yahtzee box and although it does score something, it is not scored as a Yahtzee or Yahtzee bonus.</p>
<p>In about 3.7% of games a Yahtzee is used as a Joker and scored on Full House, Small Straight or Large Straight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vslides2_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-vslides2-6">[6]</a></sup> In most of these cases the Yahtzee box has a score of 50 and so the Yahtzee also counts as a Yahtzee bonus. In about a quarter of these cases the Yahtzee box has a score 0 and so there is no Yahtzee bonus.</p>
<p>Although the average score is 254.59 the <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">Median</a> score is 248<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vslides2_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-vslides2-6">[6]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mode_(statistics)" title="Mode (statistics)">Mode</a> is 266 which occurs 1.26% of the time. The 1st <a href="/wiki/Percentile" title="Percentile">Percentile</a> is 151 (i.e. 1% of scores are 151 or less) while the 99th Percentile is 473 (i.e. 99% of scores are 473 or less).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_round">First round</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: First round">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Source:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vancura_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-vancura-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The strategy for the first round described here is based on that used by the "Optimal" strategy. Sometimes there are two possible plays which are almost equally good. In these cases the simplest option is given, i.e. the one that follows the general rules.</p>
<p>Although there are 7776 different ways of throwing 5 dice, because the order of the dice is not important there are only 252 different combinations. To use the strategy described therefore requires knowing 756 different situations.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_and_third_roll_choices">Second and third roll choices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Second and third roll choices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The general principle after the first and second throws is to keep the largest number of similar dice and rethrow the rest. When a player has a full house he will keep the three-of-a-kind. When you have two pairs keep the higher pair and rethrow the other three dice. If you have a large straight, keep it. If you have a small straight, keep it and re-roll the fifth die. If all the dice are different and there is no straight, keep just the 5. There are a number of exceptions to these rules. These exceptions are different for the second and third rolls.</p>
<p>Exceptions before the second roll:</p>
<ul>
<li>with a full house containing three 1s, he will keep all the dice and put in the Full House box.</li>
<li>with 12344 he will keep the pair not the small straight.</li>
<li>with a 3456 and a pair he will keep the pair not the small straight.</li>
<li>with a pair of 1s he will keep, in order of preference, 345, 5, 4 or 6, not the pair of 1s.</li>
</ul>
<p>So, before the second roll he will never keep two pairs, he will never keep a pair of 1s and he will never throw all the dice again.</p>
<p>Exceptions before the third roll:</p>
<ul>
<li>with a full house containing three 1s, three 2s or three 3s, he will keep all the dice and put in the Full House box.</li>
<li>with a pair of 1s and a pair of 2s or with a pair of 1s and a pair of 3s, he will keep both pairs.</li>
<li>with 11345 he will keep 345 not the pair.</li>
<li>with 12456 he will keep 456 not just the 5.</li>
</ul>
<p>So there are specific differences compared to the second roll. Now he will keep the Full House if the three-of-a-kind is 2 or 3 and keep two pairs when they are 1 and 2 or 1 and 3.He will Keep all large and small straights.He will Normally keep a pair of 1s (although 345 is still better) and keep 456 rather than 5 when all the dice are different.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Category_choice">Category choice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Category choice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In about 80% of games a player will either have at least a 3-of-a-kind or a straight. If he has any of the following he will put it in the appropriate Lower Section box: Yahtzee, full house, large straight, small straight. With a 4-of-a-kind or 3-of-a-kind he will put it in the appropriate Upper Section box. The only exception is that when he has a 3-of-a-kind where the sum of the dice is 25 or more he should use the 3-of-a-kind box. The 4-of-a-kind box is never used in the first round.</p>
<p>In the remaining 20% of cases he will have a poor hand: two pairs, one pair or all dice different. In these situations there is no appealing option, the choice being between using an Upper Section box and using Chance. With two pairs follow the rule for the lower of the two pairs he has. The rule depends on whether his pair (or smaller pair) is low (1, 2 or 3) or high (4, 5 or 6):</p>
<ul>
<li>with a low pair he will use the appropriate Upper Section box (1s, 2s or 3s) unless the sum of the dice is 22 or more in which case use the Chance box.</li>
<li>with a high pair he will use the 1s box unless the sum of the dice is 20 or more in which case use the Chance box. The only exception is that with 23446 he should use the Chance box even though it only scores 19.</li>
<li>with all dice different he will use the 1s box.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Best_and_worst_outcome">Best and worst outcome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Best and worst outcome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The best outcome in the first round is to throw a Yahtzee and put it in the Yahtzee box. This increases the final expected score from 254.59 to 320.84.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vslides2_6-6"><a href="#cite_note-vslides2-6">[6]</a></sup> Putting a Yahtzee of 6s in the 6s box results in an expected score of just 279.48. The second best outcome is to score 24 in the 6s box. This has a value of 268.23.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vslides2_6-7"><a href="#cite_note-vslides2-6">[6]</a></sup> Putting 56666 in the 4-of-a-kind box has a value of 264.54.</p>
<p>The worst first roll is 11236 which has a value of 249.83.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vslides2_6-8"><a href="#cite_note-vslides2-6">[6]</a></sup> After the second roll the worst position is 12356 which then has a value of 244.91. The worst third roll is 23446 which has a value of 238.96 when put in the Chance box.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vslides2_6-9"><a href="#cite_note-vslides2-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Extreme_scores">Extreme scores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Extreme scores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maximum_score">Maximum score</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Maximum score">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The highest possible score is 1,575 and involves throwing 13 Yahtzees, scoring 12 Yahtzee bonuses of 100 points each, as well as 375 in the other categories.</p>
<p>The 375 is achieved by scoring five aces (5), five twos (10), five threes (15), five fours (20), five fives (25), five sixes (30), the Upper Section bonus (35), five sixes scored as Three-of-a-kind (30), five sixes scored as a Four-of-a-kind (30), a Full House (25), a Small Straight (30), a Large Straight (40), a Yahtzee (50), and five sixes scored as Chance (30). The score of 1,575 requires using the "Joker" rules for the Full House, Small Straight and Large Straight categories.</p>
<p>In order to score 1,575 the player must throw 13 successive Yahtzees. The probability of getting a Yahtzee, if that is your sole objective, is 4.60% and so the probability of a player rolling 13 Yahtzees in a row (if that was their sole objective) is 4.60% raised to the 13th power or <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">6982416000000000000♠</span>4.16<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>−18</sup></span>. The probability of scoring 1,575 (if that was your sole objective) is less than this since to score the maximum you would need at least one of each number (after the first round) to fill the Upper Section and a further three 6 Yahtzees to score 30 in the Three-of-a-kind, Four-of-a-kind and Chance categories. In about 18% of Yahtzees the player has some choice over the dice to keep. This most frequently happens when a player rolls two pairs. This means that a player can slightly increase the chance of getting a 6 Yahtzee without reducing the chance of getting a Yahtzee.</p>
<p>In normal gameplay the probability of scoring 1,575 is considerably less. Using the strategy that maximizes the average score, the probability of scoring 1,575 is <span class="nowrap"><span class="sortkey" style="display:none">6980137999999999999♠</span>1.38<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>−20</sup></span>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_high_scores">Other high scores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Other high scores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For a player following the strategy which maximises the chance of getting a Yahtzee, the probability of scoring a particular number of Yahtzees follows a <a href="/wiki/Binomial_distribution" title="Binomial distribution">binomial distribution</a> and is shown in the following table.</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">

</tr>

<td>45.80%</td>

</tr>
<tr>

</tr>

<td>1 in 47,500,000</td>

<p>A player must throw at least 8 Yahtzees in order to score 1000. Throwing 8 Yahtzees will score 750 for the Yahtzee and Yahtzee bonuses. The 7 Yahtzees after the first throw will generally score highly, including the opportunity of using the Joker rule to score in, for instance, the Large Straight category. This means that a player throwing 8 Yahtzees will often be able to score 1,000.</p>
<p>In normal gameplay the probability of scoring this number of Yahtzees is considerably less. The following table shows the probability of getting certain scores using the "Optimal" strategy.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minimum_score">Minimum score</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Minimum score">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The lowest possible score is 5. The Chance box always scores the sum of the dice, so that a minimum of 5 must be scored in that category.</p>
<p>The strategy that works to maximize the average <a href="/wiki/Expected_value" title="Expected value">expected</a> score will under worst case conditions score a minimum of 12 points, but cautious play will guarantee a minimum score of 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-win_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-win-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>A score of 18 will be achieved if 11223 is thrown each round and then, whatever is re-thrown, getting 11223 again after the second and third throws, scoring 2 in the 1s box, 4 in the 2s box, 3 in the 3s box and 9 for the Chance category.</p>
<p>Scoring the minimum of 12, when attempting to maximise the average score, is less likely than scoring the maximum of 1,575 but is theoretically possible. Suppose that in the first two rounds 12355 after each roll. This would happen if a 12355 is thrown on the first roll and then, whatever dice are re-thrown, getting the same combination again; for instance, keeping 55, rethrowing the 123, and still get 12355. The optimal strategy will use the 1s box in the first round, scoring 1, and the 2s box in the second round, scoring 2. Now suppose that for the next 3 rounds you have 11226 after each roll. Again this is possible since you may throw 11226 on the first roll and then get the same when you re-throw some of dice. The optimal strategy will use the four-of-a-kind and Yahtzees boxes in the third and fourth rounds and then the 3s box in the fifth round, scoring 0 each time. For the last 8 rounds suppose you have 11223 after each roll. You will score 0 in all the remaining categories except Chance where you will score 9, giving a total of 12.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_versions">Commercial versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Commercial versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deluxe_and_collector_editions">Deluxe and collector editions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Deluxe and collector editions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Deluxe edition games have been sold alongside the regular issue games since the early 1960s. They all contain components that are more luxurious than standard game parts. In recent years, a number of collector issue Yahtzees have been sold as well. Some of these collector issues have dice that replace the pips with certain symbols connected to a theme, but still correspond to the numbers one to six.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Travel_Yahtzee">Travel Yahtzee</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Travel Yahtzee">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Travel_Yahtzee_1986.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="518" data-file-width="598" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/de/Travel_Yahtzee_1986.jpg/200px-Travel_Yahtzee_1986.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/de/Travel_Yahtzee_1986.jpg/300px-Travel_Yahtzee_1986.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/de/Travel_Yahtzee_1986.jpg/400px-Travel_Yahtzee_1986.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Travel_Yahtzee_1986.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1986 Travel Yahtzee</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the 1970s, Travel Yahtzee has been sold in various forms as part of Milton Bradley's line of travel games.</p>
<ul>
<li>In the past, the travel form of Yahtzee was composed of the five dice contained in a special apparatus (see image at the right). "Rolling" the dice is initiated by turning the apparatus over, running it on one hand and turning the apparatus upright to see the faces of the dice. Dice to be saved for the next roll are locked by snapping the reverse of the apparatus.</li>
<li>Currently, a zip-up cloth deluxe folio edition is sold. It consists of the set of dice, the cup, the scorecards, and a tray for the dice to roll on, which includes a holder for the dice to be saved for the next roll. The cup has an oblong lip for easy storage.</li>
<li>In addition to the game folio, Hasbro also released Yahtzee to Go. It comes with a dice cup that stores the dice &amp; contents. similar to the original Travel Yahtzee only without the apparatus. This is sold in tandem with the game folio.</li>
<li>There also exists a red circular travel edition, which includes the dice and scorecards, as well as a collapsible cup and detachable dice holder. The bottom half of the case acts as a dice tray. It should be noted that this one uses a different logo from the standard one (the name of the game in uppercase with an exclamation point in front of a green oval) and it is sold outside of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-images-amazon_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-images-amazon-9">[9]</a></sup></li>
<li>There are also miniature versions of the game, sold in sets contained either in cups that act as keychains (by the company Basic Fun) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ultimatekeychains_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-ultimatekeychains-10">[10]</a></sup> or in specially shaped pens (by the company Stylus).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronic_versions">Electronic versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Electronic versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Various Yahtzee console games have been sold over the years including an early version on the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Instruments_TI-99/4A" title="Texas Instruments TI-99/4A">TI-99 4A computer</a>. In 1996, the game was first released to PC and Mac users by <a href="/wiki/Atari" title="Atari">Atari</a>. The <i>Ultimate Yahtzee</i> CD-ROM game contained standard Yahtzee as well as other varieties. Later, <a href="/wiki/GameHouse" title="GameHouse">GameHouse</a> also released an authorized special version of the game for Windows users.</p>
<p>There are also several electronic versions of the game such as a handheld <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LCD" title="LCD">LCD</a> version, and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cell_phone" title="Cell phone">cell phone</a> version called <i>Yahtzee Deluxe</i>, which feature the original rules along with Duplicate and Rainbow modes, as well as independently produced versions for the <a href="/wiki/Palm_OS" title="Palm OS">Palm OS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pocket_PC" title="Pocket PC">Pocket PC</a> and several cellphone models. The version for the Nintendo Game Boy was licensed from Hasbro and was produced by DSI Games and Black Lantern Studios Inc. It was sold in a three pack that included <a href="/wiki/The_Game_of_Life" title="The Game of Life">Life</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pay_Day_(board_game)" title="Pay Day (board game)">Payday</a>, and Yahtzee. The game has also been released for the <a href="/wiki/IPod" title="IPod">iPod</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPod_touch" title="IPod touch">iPod touch</a> and the <a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a>, to be purchased through the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> as well as Google Play. Both the <a class="external text" href="https://itunes.apple.com/us/app/yahtzee-with-buddies/id967422975?mt=8" rel="nofollow">iOS App</a> and the <a class="external text" href="https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.withbuddies.yahtzee" rel="nofollow">Android App</a> are published by <a class="external text" href="http://www.scopely.com" rel="nofollow">Scopely</a>. Yahtzee is available on the <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Family_Game_Night" title="Family Game Night">Family Game Night</a></i> game by Hasbro. <a href="/wiki/Pogo.com" title="Pogo.com">Pogo.com</a> released a version in 2009, and the game is also available on the Pogo Facebook site as well.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Related_games">Related games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Related games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Games_related_to_Yahtzee" title="Games related to Yahtzee">Games related to Yahtzee</a></div>
<p>A number of related games under the Yahtzee brand have been produced. They all commonly use dice as the primary tool for gameplay, but all differ generally. The first was Triple Yahtzee, developed in 1972. The game has inspired two short-lived <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a> <a href="/wiki/Game_show" title="Game show">game shows</a>: 1975's <i><a href="/wiki/Spin-Off_(game_show)" title="Spin-Off (game show)">Spin-Off</a></i> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CBS_(network)" title="CBS (network)">CBS</a> and 1988's syndicated <i><a href="/wiki/Yahtzee_(game_show)" title="Yahtzee (game show)">Yahtzee</a></i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_versions">Online versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Online versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are a large number of versions of Yahtzee which can be played online or are available to download.</p>
<ul>
<li>"Open Yahtzee" is a cross-platform open-source (free) version of Yahtzee for one player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-openyahtzee_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-openyahtzee-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Similar_games">Similar games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Similar games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are a large number of related games. <a href="/wiki/Yatzy" title="Yatzy">Yatzy</a> is one of the most popular. Yatzy rules and scoring categories are somewhat different from Yahtzee:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The bonus for reaching 63 or more points in the Upper Section is normally 50 points.</li>
<li>There are two extra boxes for the "One Pair" and "Two Pair" categories. These score the total of the pair(s) involved. For instance, 5-5-4-4-1 will score 10 points in the One Pair box and 18 in the Two Pair box. In the Two Pair category, the pairs must be different.</li>
<li>The Three-of-a-Kind and Four-of-a-Kind categories are scored using the total of the needed number of same-faced dice. For instance, 5-5-5-5-6 will score 20 points in Four-of-a-Kind and 15 points in Three-of-a-Kind. This scoring rule is the same as the Four-of-a-Kind scoring used in <a href="/wiki/Yacht_(dice_game)" title="Yacht (dice game)">Yacht</a>.</li>
<li>Full House scores the total of all dice, as in Yacht.</li>
<li>Small Straight and Large Straight have the same definitions as in Yacht. A Small Straight is 1-2-3-4-5 and scores 15 points (the total of the dice faces); the Large Straight is 2-3-4-5-6 and scores 20 points (again the combined value of the dice).</li>
<li>There are no Yahtzee bonuses or Joker rule. Yahtzees can be scored in other categories under the normal scoring rules. For example, a Yahtzee of sixes will score 12 in the One Pair box, 18 in Three-of-a-Kind, 24 in Four-of-a-Kind, 30 in Sixes or Chance and 0 in Two Pair, Full House, Small Straight and Large Straight boxes.</li>
</ul>
<p>Other related games include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Balut_(game)" title="Balut (game)">Balut</a> is the name of a Danish dice game played by expatriates in many countries all over the world. The name of the game is taken from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balut_(egg)" title="Balut (egg)">balut</a> eggs.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kismet_(dice_game)" title="Kismet (dice game)">Kismet</a> has dice with multiple colors. Both numbers and colors are taken into account when scoring.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yahtzee&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ben_%22Yahtzee%22_Croshaw" title='Ben "Yahtzee" Croshaw'>Ben "Yahtzee" Croshaw</a> is a British video games critic currently based in Australia who takes his pseudonym from the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-escapistmagazine_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-escapistmagazine-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li>Yahtzee has been cited as a precipitating factor in a case of domestic violence <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and as the motive for at least one murder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kare11_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-kare11-18">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li>The word "Yahtzee" has been used to exclaim excitement when a University of Kentucky football recruit commits to attending the school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-courier-journal_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-courier-journal-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li>The tennis player Andy Roddick, after winning a match in which events seemed to go his way, said, in an interview, that everything was "coming up Yahtzee".</li>
</ul>
